<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Damage_to_human_health">Damage to human health<span class="anchor" id="Health_effects"></span></span></h2>
<p>The use of coal as fuel causes ill health and deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Mining and processing of coal causes air and water pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-132">[132]</a></sup> Coal-powered plants emit nitrogen oxides, sulfur dioxide, particulate pollution and heavy metals, which adversely affect human health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-132">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coalbed_methane_extraction" title="Coalbed methane extraction">Coal bed methane extraction</a> is important to avoid mining accidents.
</p><p>The deadly <a href="/wiki/Pea_soup_fog#London" title="Pea soup fog">London smog</a> was caused primarily by the heavy use of coal. Globally coal is estimated to cause 800,000 premature deaths every year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Endcoal_health_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Endcoal_health-133">[133]</a></sup> mostly in India<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economist2018_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Economist2018-134">[134]</a></sup> and China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p><p>Burning coal is a major emitter of <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a>, which creates PM2.5 <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">particulates</a>, the most dangerous form of air pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>Coal smokestack emissions cause <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strokes" title="Strokes">strokes</a>, reduced <a href="/wiki/Intelligence" title="Intelligence">intelligence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artery" title="Artery">artery</a> blockages, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_attacks" title="Heart attacks">heart attacks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congestive_heart_failure" title="Congestive heart failure">congestive heart failure</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiac_arrhythmias" title="Cardiac arrhythmias">cardiac arrhythmias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercury_poisoning" title="Mercury poisoning">mercury poisoning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stenosis" title="Stenosis">arterial occlusion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lung_cancer" title="Lung cancer">lung cancer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-psr_coal-damages-health_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-psr_coal-damages-health-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>Annual health costs in Europe from use of coal to generate electricity are estimated at up to €43 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>In China, improvements to air quality and human health would increase with more stringent climate policies, mainly because the country's energy is so heavily reliant on coal. And there would be a net economic benefit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2017 study in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_Journal" title="Economic Journal">Economic Journal</a></i> found that for Britain during the period 1851–1860, "a one standard deviation increase in coal use raised infant mortality by 6–8% and that industrial coal use explains roughly one-third of the urban mortality penalty observed during this period."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>Breathing in <a href="/wiki/Coal_dust" title="Coal dust">coal dust</a> causes <a href="/wiki/Coalworker%27s_pneumoconiosis" title="Coalworker's pneumoconiosis">coalworker's pneumoconiosis</a> or "black lung", so called because the coal dust literally turns the lungs black from their usual pink color.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> In the United States alone, it is estimated that 1,500 former employees of the coal industry die every year from the effects of breathing in coal mine dust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>
</p><p>Huge amounts of coal ash and other waste is produced annually. Use of coal generates hundreds of millions of tons of ash and other waste products every year. These include <a href="/wiki/Fly_ash" title="Fly ash">fly ash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bottom_ash" title="Bottom ash">bottom ash</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Flue-gas_desulfurization" title="Flue-gas desulfurization">flue-gas desulfurization</a> sludge, that contain <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">mercury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thorium" title="Thorium">thorium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arsenic" title="Arsenic">arsenic</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metals" title="Heavy metals">heavy metals</a>, along with non-metals such as <a href="/wiki/Selenium" title="Selenium">selenium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup>
</p><p>Around 10% of coal is ash:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_ash" title="Coal ash">coal ash</a> is hazardous and toxic to human beings and some other living things.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Coal ash contains the radioactive elements <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thorium" title="Thorium">thorium</a>. Coal ash and other solid combustion byproducts are stored locally and escape in various ways that expose those living near coal plants to radiation and environmental toxics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sa-coal-ash-more-rdactiv_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-sa-coal-ash-more-rdactiv-149">[149]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Damage_to_the_environment">Damage to the environment</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_the_coal_industry" title="Environmental impact of the coal industry">Environmental impact of the coal industry</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="828" decoding="async" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg/220px-Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg/330px-Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg/440px-Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_ash_slide_site_Dec_23_2008_TVA.gov_123002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial photograph of the site of the <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Fossil_Plant" title="Kingston Fossil Plant">Kingston Fossil Plant</a> coal fly ash slurry spill taken the day after <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Fossil_Plant_coal_fly_ash_slurry_spill" title="Kingston Fossil Plant coal fly ash slurry spill">the event</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Coal_mining" title="Coal mining">Coal mining</a> and coal fueling of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_stations" title="Power stations">power stations</a> and industrial processes can cause major environmental damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p><p>Water systems are affected by coal mining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> For example, mining affects <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_table" title="Water table">water table</a> levels and acidity. Spills of fly ash, such as the <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Fossil_Plant_coal_fly_ash_slurry_spill" title="Kingston Fossil Plant coal fly ash slurry spill">Kingston Fossil Plant coal fly ash slurry spill</a>, can also contaminate land and waterways, and destroy homes. Power stations that burn coal also consume large quantities of water. This can affect the flows of rivers, and has consequential impacts on other land uses. In areas of <a href="/wiki/Water_scarcity" title="Water scarcity">water scarcity</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Thar_Desert" title="Thar Desert">Thar Desert</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, coal mining and coal power plants would use significant quantities of water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the earliest known impacts of coal on the <a href="/wiki/Water_cycle" title="Water cycle">water cycle</a> was <a href="/wiki/Acid_rain" title="Acid rain">acid rain</a>. In 2014 approximately 100 <a href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude_(mass)#106_to_1011_kg" title="Orders of magnitude (mass)">Tg</a>/S of <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> (SO<sub>2</sub>) was released, over half of which was from burning coal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> After release, the sulfur dioxide is oxidized to H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> which scatters solar radiation, hence its increase in the atmosphere exerts a cooling effect on climate. This beneficially masks some of the warming caused by increased greenhouse gases. However, the sulfur is precipitated out of the atmosphere as acid rain in a matter of weeks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> whereas carbon dioxide remains in the atmosphere for hundreds of years. Release of SO<sub>2</sub> also contributes to the widespread acidification of ecosystems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>Disused coal mines can also cause issues. Subsidence can occur above tunnels, causing damage to infrastructure or cropland. Coal mining can also cause long lasting fires, and it has been estimated that thousands of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_seam_fire" title="Coal seam fire">coal seam fires</a> are burning at any given time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deep_underground_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deep_underground-156">[156]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Brennender_Berg" title="Brennender Berg">Brennender Berg</a> has been burning since 1668 and is still burning in the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mineralienatlas_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-mineralienatlas-157">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p>The production of coke from coal produces <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">ammonia</a>, coal tar, and gaseous compounds as byproducts which if discharged to land, air or waterways can pollute the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whyalla_steelworks" title="Whyalla steelworks">Whyalla steelworks</a> is one example of a coke producing facility where liquid ammonia was discharged to the marine environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emission_intensity">Emission intensity</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Emission_intensity" title="Emission intensity">Emission intensity</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life-cycle_greenhouse-gas_emissions_of_energy_sources" title="Life-cycle greenhouse-gas emissions of energy sources">greenhouse gas emitted over the life of a generator</a> per unit of electricity generated. The emission intensity of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_power_station" title="Coal power station">coal power stations</a> is high, as they emit around 1000 g of CO<sub>2</sub>eq for each kWh generated, while natural gas is medium-emission intensity at around 500 g CO<sub>2</sub>eq per kWh. The emission intensity of coal varies with type and generator technology and exceeds 1200 g per kWh in some countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Underground_fires">Underground fires</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coal-seam_fire" title="Coal-seam fire">Coal-seam fire</a></div>
<p>Thousands of coal fires are burning around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Those burning underground can be difficult to locate and many cannot be extinguished. Fires can cause the ground above to subside, their combustion gases are dangerous to life, and breaking out to the surface can initiate surface <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">wildfires</a>. Coal seams can be set on fire by <a href="/wiki/Spontaneous_combustion" title="Spontaneous combustion">spontaneous combustion</a> or contact with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mine_fire" title="Mine fire">mine fire</a> or surface fire. Lightning strikes are an important source of ignition. The coal continues to burn slowly back into the seam until oxygen (air) can no longer reach the flame front. A grass fire in a coal area can set dozens of coal seams on fire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Coal fires in China burn an estimated 120 million tons of coal a year, emitting 360 million metric tons of CO<sub>2</sub>, amounting to 2–3% of the annual worldwide production of CO<sub>2</sub> from <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Centralia,_Pennsylvania" title="Centralia, Pennsylvania">Centralia, Pennsylvania</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Borough_(Pennsylvania)" title="Borough (Pennsylvania)">borough</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Coal_Region" title="Coal Region">Coal Region</a> of the United States), an exposed vein of anthracite ignited in 1962 due to a trash fire in the borough landfill, located in an abandoned <a href="/wiki/Anthracite" title="Anthracite">anthracite</a> <a href="/wiki/Surface_mining" title="Surface mining">strip mine</a> pit. Attempts to extinguish the fire were unsuccessful, and it <a href="/wiki/Centralia_mine_fire" title="Centralia mine fire">continues to burn underground to this day</a>. The Australian <a href="/wiki/Burning_Mountain" title="Burning Mountain">Burning Mountain</a> was originally believed to be a volcano, but the smoke and ash come from a coal fire that has been burning for some 6,000 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>At Kuh i Malik in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yagnob_Valley" title="Yagnob Valley">Yagnob Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>, coal deposits have been burning for thousands of years, creating vast underground labyrinths full of unique minerals, some of them very beautiful.
</p><p>The reddish siltstone rock that caps many ridges and buttes in the <a href="/wiki/Powder_River_Basin" title="Powder River Basin">Powder River Basin</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> and in western <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a> is called <i>porcelanite</i>, which resembles the coal burning waste "clinker" or volcanic "<a href="/wiki/Scoria" title="Scoria">scoria</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Clinker is rock that has been fused by the natural burning of coal. In the Powder River Basin approximately 27 to 54 billion tons of coal burned within the past three million years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Wild coal fires in the area were reported by the <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Clark_Expedition" title="Lewis and Clark Expedition">Lewis and Clark Expedition</a> as well as explorers and settlers in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span></h3>
<p>The largest and most long-term effect of coal use is the release of carbon dioxide, a <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> that causes <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. Coal-fired power plants were the single largest contributor to the growth in global CO<sub>2</sub> emissions in 2018,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gençsü_2019,_p._8_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gençsü_2019,_p._8-170">[170]</a></sup> 40% of the total fossil fuel emissions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phys2018_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-phys2018-8">[8]</a></sup> and more than a quarter of total emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cebf_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-cebf-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[note 1]</a></sup> Coal mining can emit methane, another greenhouse gas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016 world gross <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_emissions" title="Carbon dioxide emissions">carbon dioxide emissions</a> from coal usage were 14.5 gigatonnes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> For every megawatt-hour generated, coal-fired electric power generation emits around a tonne of carbon dioxide, which is double the approximately 500 kg of carbon dioxide released by a <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>-fired electric plant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup> In 2013, the head of the UN climate agency advised that most of the world's coal reserves should be left in the ground to avoid catastrophic global warming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup> To keep global warming below 1.5 °C or 2 °C hundreds, or possibly thousands, of coal-fired power plants will need to be retired early.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution_mitigation">Pollution mitigation</span></h2>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><div class="excerpt">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Figure_1-_Sample_Layout_of_Emissions_Controls_at_a_Coal_Power_Plant_(7315637538)_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="963" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Figure_1-_Sample_Layout_of_Emissions_Controls_at_a_Coal_Power_Plant_%287315637538%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Figure_1-_Sample_Layout_of_Emissions_Controls_at_a_Coal_Power_Plant_%287315637538%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Figure_1-_Sample_Layout_of_Emissions_Controls_at_a_Coal_Power_Plant_%287315637538%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/495px-Figure_1-_Sample_Layout_of_Emissions_Controls_at_a_Coal_Power_Plant_%287315637538%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Figure_1-_Sample_Layout_of_Emissions_Controls_at_a_Coal_Power_Plant_%287315637538%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/660px-Figure_1-_Sample_Layout_of_Emissions_Controls_at_a_Coal_Power_Plant_%287315637538%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Figure_1-_Sample_Layout_of_Emissions_Controls_at_a_Coal_Power_Plant_(7315637538)_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Emissions controls at a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_fired_power_plant" title="Coal fired power plant">coal fired power plant</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">These paragraphs are an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Coal_pollution_mitigation" title="Coal pollution mitigation">Coal pollution mitigation</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Coal_pollution_mitigation&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Coal_pollution_mitigation" title="Coal pollution mitigation">Coal pollution mitigation</a>, sometimes called clean coal, is a series of systems and technologies that seek to mitigate the <a href="/wiki/Health_and_environmental_impact_of_the_coal_industry" title="Health and environmental impact of the coal industry">health and environmental impact of coal</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coal_pollution_mitigation_NatGeoMyth_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coal_pollution_mitigation_NatGeoMyth-178">[177]</a></sup> in particular <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> from <a href="/wiki/Coal-fired_power_station" title="Coal-fired power station">coal-fired power stations</a>, and from coal burnt by <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industry</a>.
</p>
The primary focus is on <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1060974363">.mw-parser-output .template-chem2-su{display:inline-block;font-size:80%;line-height:1;vertical-align:-0.35em}.mw-parser-output .template-chem2-su>span{display:block}.mw-parser-output sub.template-chem2-sub{font-size:80%;vertical-align:-0.35em}.mw-parser-output sup.template-chem2-sup{font-size:80%;vertical-align:0.65em}</style><span class="chemf nowrap">SO<sub class="template-chem2-sub">2</sub></span>) and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxides</a> (<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1060974363" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="chemf nowrap">NO<sub class="template-chem2-sub"><i>x</i></sub></span>), the most important gases which caused <a href="/wiki/Acid_rain" title="Acid rain">acid rain</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">particulates</a> which cause visible air pollution, illness and premature deaths. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1060974363" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="chemf nowrap">SO<sub class="template-chem2-sub">2</sub></span> can be removed by <a href="/wiki/Flue-gas_desulfurization" title="Flue-gas desulfurization">flue-gas desulfurization</a> and <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1060974363" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="chemf nowrap">NO<sub class="template-chem2-sub">2</sub></span> by <a href="/wiki/Selective_catalytic_reduction" title="Selective catalytic reduction">selective catalytic reduction</a> (SCR). Particulates can be removed with <a href="/wiki/Electrostatic_precipitator" title="Electrostatic precipitator">electrostatic precipitators</a>. Although perhaps less efficient, <a href="/wiki/Wet_scrubber" title="Wet scrubber">wet scrubbers</a> can remove both gases and particulates. Reducing <a href="/wiki/Fly_ash" title="Fly ash">fly ash</a> reduces emissions of <a href="/wiki/Naturally_occurring_radioactive_material" title="Naturally occurring radioactive material">radioactive materials</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">Mercury</a> emissions can be reduced up to 95%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Carbon_capture_and_storage" title="Carbon capture and storage">capturing carbon dioxide emissions</a> from coal is generally not economically viable.</div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Standards">Standards</span></h3>
<p>Local pollution standards include GB13223-2011 (China), India,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Emissions_Directive" title="Industrial Emissions Directive">Industrial Emissions Directive</a> (EU) and the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act (United States)</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_monitoring">Satellite monitoring</span></h3>
<p>Satellite monitoring is now used to crosscheck national data, for example <a href="/wiki/Sentinel-5_Precursor" title="Sentinel-5 Precursor">Sentinel-5 Precursor</a> has shown that Chinese control of SO<sub>2</sub> has only been partially successful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> It has also revealed that low use of technology such as SCR has resulted in high NO<sub>2</sub> emissions in South Africa and India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Combined_cycle_power_plants">Combined cycle power plants</span></h3>
<p>A few <a href="/wiki/Integrated_gasification_combined_cycle" title="Integrated gasification combined cycle">Integrated gasification combined cycle</a> (IGCC) coal-fired power plants have been built with <a href="/wiki/Coal_gasification" title="Coal gasification">coal gasification</a>. Although they burn coal more efficiently and therefore emit less pollution, the technology has not generally proved economically viable for coal, except possibly in Japan although this is controversial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carbon_capture_and_storage">Carbon capture and storage</span></h3>
<p>Although still being intensively researched and considered economically viable for some uses other than with coal; <a href="/wiki/Carbon_capture_and_storage" title="Carbon capture and storage">carbon capture and storage</a> has been tested at the <a href="/wiki/Petra_Nova" title="Petra Nova">Petra Nova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boundary_Dam_Power_Station" title="Boundary Dam Power Station">Boundary Dam</a> coal-fired power plants and has been found to be technically feasible but not economically viable for use with coal, due to reductions in the cost of solar PV technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span></h2>
<p>In 2018 <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$80 billion</span> was invested in coal supply but almost all for sustaining production levels rather than opening new mines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup>
In the long term coal and oil could cost the world trillions of dollars per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> Coal alone may cost Australia billions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup> whereas costs to some smaller companies or cities could be on the scale of millions of dollars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> The economies most damaged by coal (via climate change) may be India and the US as they are the countries with the highest <a href="/wiki/Social_cost_of_carbon" title="Social cost of carbon">social cost of carbon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup> Bank loans to finance coal are a risk to the Indian economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economist2018_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-Economist2018-134">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>China is the largest producer of coal in the world. It is the world's largest energy consumer, and <a href="/wiki/Coal_in_China" title="Coal in China">coal in China</a> supplies 60% of its primary energy. However two fifths of China's coal power stations are estimated to be loss-making.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CarbTrk2018_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-CarbTrk2018-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p><p>Air pollution from coal storage and handling costs the US almost 200 dollars for every extra ton stored, due to PM2.5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> Coal pollution costs the €43 billion each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> Measures to cut air pollution benefit individuals financially and the economies of countries<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> such as China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidies">Subsidies</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Fossil fuel subsidies">Fossil fuel subsidies</a></div>
<p>Subsidies for coal in 2021 have been estimated at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$19 billion</span>, not including electricity subsidies, and are expected to rise in 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Coal&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> countries provide at least <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$63.9 billion</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gençsü_2019,_p._8_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gençsü_2019,_p._8-170">[170]</a></sup> of government support per year for the production of coal, including coal-fired power: many subsidies are impossible to quantify<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClimateTransparency2019_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-ClimateTransparency2019-198">[197]</a></sup> but they include <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$27.6 billion</span> in domestic and international public finance, <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$15.4 billion</span> in fiscal support, and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$20.9 billion</span> in state-owned enterprise (SOE) investments per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gençsü_2019,_p._8_170-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gençsü_2019,_p._8-170">[170]</a></sup> In the EU state aid to new coal-fired plants is banned from 2020, and to existing coal-fired plants from 2025.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> As of 2018, government funding for new coal power plants was supplied by <a href="/wiki/Exim_Bank_of_China" title="Exim Bank of China">Exim Bank of China</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urgewald_2018_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-Urgewald_2018-200">[199]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Bank_for_International_Cooperation" title="Japan Bank for International Cooperation">Japan Bank for International Cooperation</a> and Indian public sector banks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Kazakhstan#Coal" title="Energy in Kazakhstan">Coal in Kazakhstan</a> was the main recipient of coal consumption subsidies totalling US$2 billion in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coal_in_Turkey#Subsidies" title="Coal in Turkey">Coal in Turkey</a> benefited from substantial subsidies in 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stranded_assets">Stranded assets</span></h3>
<p>Some coal-fired power stations could become <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stranded_assets" title="Stranded assets">stranded assets</a>, for example <a href="/wiki/China_Energy_Investment" title="China Energy Investment">China Energy Investment</a>, the world's largest power company, risks losing half its capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CarbTrk2018_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-CarbTrk2018-118">[118]</a></sup> However, state-owned electricity utilities such as <a href="/wiki/Eskom" title="Eskom">Eskom</a> in South Africa, <a href="/wiki/Perusahaan_Listrik_Negara" title="Perusahaan Listrik Negara">Perusahaan Listrik Negara</a> in Indonesia, <a href="/wiki/Sarawak_Energy" title="Sarawak Energy">Sarawak Energy</a> in Malaysia, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipower" title="Taipower">Taipower</a> in Taiwan, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EGAT" title="EGAT">EGAT</a> in Thailand, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_Electricity" title="Vietnam Electricity">Vietnam Electricity</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E%C3%9CA%C5%9E" title="EÜAŞ">EÜAŞ</a> in Turkey are building or planning new plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Urgewald_2018b_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-Urgewald_2018b-204">[203]</a></sup> As of 2021 this may be helping to cause a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_bubble" title="Carbon bubble">carbon bubble</a> which could cause financial instability if it bursts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<p>Countries building or financing new coal-fired power stations, such as China, India, Indonesia, Vietnam, Turkey and Bangladesh, face mounting international criticism for obstructing the aims of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cornot-Gandolfe_2018_105-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cornot-Gandolfe_2018-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup>  In 2019, the Pacific Island nations (in particular <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>) criticized Australia for failing to cut their emissions at a faster rate than they were, citing concerns about coastal inundation and erosion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian2018_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2018-210">[209]</a></sup> In May 2021, the G7 members agreed to end new direct government support for international coal power generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_coal">Opposition to coal</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_(25563929593).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg/220px-Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg/330px-Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg/440px-Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_%2825563929593%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coral_not_coal_protest_at_India_Finance_Minister_Arun_Jaitley_Visit_to_Australia_(25563929593).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protesting against damage to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Barrier_Reef" title="Great Barrier Reef">Great Barrier Reef</a> caused by <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Australia" title="Climate change in Australia">climate change in Australia</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gemeinsam_stark,Hambacher_Forst,NRW.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg/220px-Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg/330px-Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg/440px-Gemeinsam_stark%2CHambacher_Forst%2CNRW.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gemeinsam_stark,Hambacher_Forst,NRW.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tree houses erected to protest against the felling of part of <a href="/wiki/Hambach_Forest" title="Hambach Forest">Hambach Forest</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Hambach_surface_mine" title="Hambach surface mine">Hambach surface mine</a> in Germany, after which the felling was suspended in 2018</div></div></div>
<p>Opposition to coal pollution was one of the main reasons the modern <a href="/wiki/Environmental_movement" title="Environmental movement">environmental movement</a> started in the 19th century.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transition_away_from_coal">Transition away from coal</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coal_phase-out" title="Coal phase-out">Coal phase-out</a></div>
<p>In order to meet global climate goals and provide power to those that do not currently have it coal power must be reduced from nearly 10,000 TWh to less than 2,000 TWh by 2040.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> Phasing out coal has short-term health and environmental benefits which exceed the costs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> but some countries still favor coal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup> and there is much disagreement about how quickly it should be phased out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup> However many countries, such as the <a href="/wiki/Powering_Past_Coal_Alliance" title="Powering Past Coal Alliance">Powering Past Coal Alliance</a>, have already or are transitioned away from coal;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[216]</a></sup> the largest transition announced so far being Germany, which is due to shut down its last coal-fired power station between 2035 and 2038.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[217]</a></sup> Some countries use the ideas of a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Just_Transition" title="Just Transition">Just Transition</a>", for example to use some of the benefits of transition to provide early pensions for coal miners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[218]</a></sup> However, low-lying <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Islands</a> are concerned the transition is not fast enough and that they will be inundated by <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a>, so they have called for <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> countries to completely phase out coal by 2030 and other countries by 2040.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian2018_210-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2018-210">[209]</a></sup> In 2020, although China built some plants, globally more coal power was retired than built: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Secretary_General" title="UN Secretary General">UN Secretary General</a> has also said that <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> countries should stop generating electricity from coal by 2030 and the rest of the world by 2040.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[219]</a></sup> Phasing down coal was agreed at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/COP26" title="COP26">COP26</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Climate_Pact" title="Glasgow Climate Pact">Glasgow Climate Pact</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peak_coal">Peak coal</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg/220px-Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg/330px-Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg/440px-Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coal_mine_Wyoming.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A coal mine in <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>, United States. The United States has the world's largest coal reserves.</div></div></div><div class="excerpt-block"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066933788" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Peak_coal" title="Peak coal">Peak coal</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Peak_coal&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Peak_coal" title="Peak coal">Peak coal</a> is the peak consumption or production of coal by a human community. Global coal consumption peaked in 2013, and had dropped slightly by the end of the 2010s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peak_coal_forbes_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peak_coal_forbes-221">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peak_coal_iea-2020_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peak_coal_iea-2020-222">[221]</a></sup> 
The peak of coal's share in the global <a href="/wiki/Energy_mix" title="Energy mix">energy mix</a> was in 2008, when coal accounted for 30% of global energy production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peak_coal_forbes_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-Peak_coal_forbes-221">[220]</a></sup> 
The decline in coal use is largely driven by consumption declines in the United States and Europe, as well as developed economies in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peak_coal_forbes_221-2"><a href="#cite_note-Peak_coal_forbes-221">[220]</a></sup> In 2019, production increases in countries such as China, Indonesia, India, Russia and Australia compensated for the falls in the United States and Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peak_coal_iea-2020_222-1"><a href="#cite_note-Peak_coal_iea-2020-222">[221]</a></sup> However, coal's structural decline continued in the 2020s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[222]</a></sup>
</p>
Peak coal can be driven by peak demand or peak supply. Historically, it was widely believed that the supply-side would eventually drive peak coal due to the depletion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_reserves" title="Coal reserves">coal reserves</a>. However, since the increasing global efforts to limit <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, peak coal has been driven by demand, which has stayed below the 2013 peak consumption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peak_coal_forbes_221-3"><a href="#cite_note-Peak_coal_forbes-221">[220]</a></sup> This is due in large part to the rapid expansion of natural gas and renewable energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peak_coal_forbes_221-4"><a href="#cite_note-Peak_coal_forbes-221">[220]</a></sup> Many countries have pledged to <a href="/wiki/Coal_phase-out" title="Coal phase-out">phase-out coal</a>, despite estimates that project coal reserves to have the capacity to last for centuries at current consumption levels. In some countries<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (January 2021)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> coal consumption may still increase in the early 2020s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[223]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Switch_to_cleaner_fuels_and_lower_carbon_electricity_generation">Switch to cleaner fuels and lower carbon electricity generation</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas#Power_generation" title="Natural gas">Natural gas § Power generation</a></div>
<p>Coal-fired generation puts out about twice as much carbon dioxide—around a tonne for every megawatt hour generated—as electricity generated by burning natural gas at 500 kg of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> per megawatt hour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[224]</a></sup> In addition to generating electricity, natural gas is also popular in some countries for heating and as an <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_vehicle" title="Natural gas vehicle">automotive fuel</a>.
</p><p>The use of <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Energy in the United Kingdom">coal in the United Kingdom</a> declined as a result of the development of <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_oil" title="North Sea oil">North Sea oil</a> and the subsequent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dash_for_gas" title="Dash for gas">dash for gas</a> during the 1990s. In Canada some <a href="/wiki/Thermal_power_station" title="Thermal power station">coal power plants</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Hearn_Generating_Station" title="Hearn Generating Station">Hearn Generating Station</a>, switched from coal to natural gas. In 2017, <a href="/wiki/Coal_power_in_the_United_States" title="Coal power in the United States">coal power in the United States</a> provided 30% of the electricity, down from approximately 49% in 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTKentucky_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTKentucky-227">[226]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[227]</a></sup> due to plentiful supplies of low cost natural gas obtained by <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_fracturing" title="Hydraulic fracturing">hydraulic fracturing</a> of tight shale formations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coal_regions_in_transition">Coal regions in transition</span></h3>
<p>Some <a href="/wiki/Coal-mining_region" title="Coal-mining region">coal-mining regions</a> are highly dependent on coal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment">Employment</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Just_Transition" title="Just Transition">Just Transition</a></div>
<p>Some coal miners are concerned their jobs may be lost in the transition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[230]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Just_transition" title="Just transition">just transition</a> from coal is supported by the <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[231]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bioremediation">Bioremediation</span></h3>
<p>The white rot fungus <i><a href="/wiki/Trametes_versicolor" title="Trametes versicolor">Trametes versicolor</a></i> can grow on and metabolize naturally occurring coal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup> The bacteria <a href="/wiki/Diplococcus" title="Diplococcus">Diplococcus</a> has been found to degrade coal, raising its temperature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[233]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_usage">Cultural usage</span></h2>
<p>Coal is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_minerals,_rocks,_stones_and_gemstones" title="List of U.S. state minerals, rocks, stones and gemstones">official state mineral</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[234]</a></sup> and the official state rock of <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup> both <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. states</a> have a historic link to coal mining.
</p><p>Some cultures hold that children who misbehave will receive only a lump of coal from <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus" title="Santa Claus">Santa Claus</a> for Christmas in their <a href="/wiki/Christmas_stocking" title="Christmas stocking">christmas stockings</a> instead of presents.
</p><p>It is also customary and considered lucky in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_of_England" title="North of England">North of England</a> to give coal as a gift on <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a>. This occurs as part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First-Foot" title="First-Foot">First-Footing</a> and represents warmth for the year to come.
</p>
